[7:0:204,253] 9658   Budget Stabilization Account  

[8:0:66,274] Proposition 2, approved by voters in November 2014, replaced the Proposition 58 (2004) version of the Budget Stabilization  

[8:1:66,285] Account (BSA) to build a stronger "rainy day" reserve while requiring accelerated debt pay down. Proposition 2 strengthened  

[8:2:66,295] the reserve by providing more stringent requirements to transfer funds back to the General Fund or suspend deposits to the  

[8:3:66,305] BSA, and increasing the reserve limit.  

[9:0:66,325] Proposition 2 requires a transfer from the General Fund to the BSA by October 1 of each year, as well as true up transfers  

[9:1:66,336] between the General Fund and the BSA for the two preceding fiscal years. In addition to the transfer to the BSA, a calculated  

[9:2:66,346] amount is appropriated for supplemental debt payments and other specified long-term liabilities.  

[10:0:66,373] LEGAL CITATIONS AND AUTHORITY  

[10:1:66,392] PROGRAM AUTHORITY  

[11:0:66,412] Section 20, Article XVI of the Constitution of the State of California.  

[11:1:66,423] Control Section 35.50, Budget Act.  

[11:2:66,440] Item 9658-011-0001, 2016 Budget Act and 2018 Budget Act.  

[12:0:66,477] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[13:0:66,497] 7760 - Proposition 2 requires the Legislature, through the 2029-30 fiscal year, to annually set aside in the BSA for a "rainy day"  

[13:1:66,507] 50 percent of the sum of 1.5 percent of estimated General Fund revenues and the amount of revenue from capital gains over 8  

[13:2:66,517] percent of General Fund tax proceeds that is not required to fund Proposition 98, and use the remaining 50 percent to pay  

[13:3:66,527] down debt. Beginning in 2030-31, 100 percent of the above sum would be deposited in the BSA for a "rainy day," reduced by  

[13:4:66,537] any amount up to 50 percent that the Legislature appropriates to pay down debt. The maximum balance in the BSA is limited to  

[13:5:66,548] 10 percent of General Fund proceeds of taxes for the fiscal year. Any amounts in excess of ten percent may only be used for  

[13:6:66,558] infrastructure needs.  

[14:0:66,578] Proposition 2 includes a true up mechanism for the two preceding years.  

[15:0:66,599] The Legislature may suspend or reduce the BSA transfer if the Governor declares a budget emergency. Withdrawal of funds  

[15:1:66,609] from the BSA is limited to half of the fund's balance unless funds in the BSA have been returned to the General Fund for  

[15:2:66,619] appropriation in the immediately preceding fiscal year.  

[16:0:66,639] Proposition 2 also establishes a Proposition 98 reserve whereby spikes in funding will be saved for future years. This will  

[16:1:66,650] smooth school spending and minimize future cuts. The Proposition 98 reserve does not change the Proposition 98 minimum  

[16:2:66,660] guarantee calculation.   See 9889 - Public School System Stabilization Account for more information on the Proposition 98  

[16:3:66,670] reserve.  

[17:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[6:0:66,261] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[6:1:66,280] 7765 - EQUITY CLAIMS  

[7:0:66,300] This program includes all claims approved by the three-member California Victim Compensation Board and the Government  

[7:1:66,310] Claims Program under the Department of General Services, and referred to the Legislature in the omnibus claims bills for  

[7:2:66,321] payment. The program provides an equitable procedure for the payment of the following categories of claims:  

[7:3:65,338] • Claims for which no appropriation has been made or for which no fund is available, but the settlement of which has been  

[7:4:76,349] provided for by statute or constitutional provision.  

[7:5:65,365] • Claims for which the appropriation made or fund designated is exhausted.  

[7:6:65,381] • Claims for which settlement is not otherwise provided for by statute or constitutional provision.  

[7:7:66,399] The Government Claims Program was transferred to the Department of General Services from the former California Victim  

[7:8:66,409] Compensation and Government Claims Board in July 2016. The California Victim Compensation and Government Claims  

[7:9:66,419] Board became the California Victim Compensation Board.  

[7:10:66,437] 7770 - SETTLEMENTS AND JUDGMENTS  

[8:0:66,457] This program includes claims paid through judgment and settlement bills sponsored by the Department of Justice each year.  

[8:1:66,467] The claims are either judgments against the state or settlements approved by the Department of Justice pursuant to the  

[8:2:66,478] authority provided in Government Code Section 948 et seq.

[12:0:164,615] 9800   Augmentation for Employee Compensation  

[13:0:66,637] This item reflects funding augmentations for state employee compensation. If the Legislature previously appropriated money,  

[13:1:66,647] through this budget item, to pay for the economic terms of employee compensation in previous fiscal years, the funding for  

[13:2:66,657] those economic terms is included in departments' budgets. When economic terms require funding not yet appropriated by the  

[13:3:66,667] Legislature, those funds are included in this budget item.  

[14:0:66,688] Additionally, this item sets aside funding for penalties the state may face under the Affordable Care Act (ACA). Beginning in  

[14:1:66,698] 2015, the state became subject to the Employer Shared Responsibility provision of the ACA. This provision requires large  

[15:0:66,708] employers to offer health benefits to full-time employees, defined as those who work on average 130 or more hours per month  

[16:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[3:0:66,83] (or 30 hours per week), and their dependent children. Under this provision, the state may be subject to penalties (Part B  

[3:1:66,93] Penalty), which may include part-time, temporary, and seasonal employees that may have been considered full-time for one or  

[3:2:66,103] more months, were not offered or did not qualify for health benefits through the state, purchased health coverage from the  

[3:3:66,113] Health Insurance Marketplace (known as Covered California), and received a premium tax credit or cost sharing reduction.  

[4:0:66,134] The ACA also contains reporting requirements, which require the state to track specified ACA-related employee information on  

[4:1:66,144] a monthly basis to identify the employees who meet health eligibility requirements, document whether benefits were offered,  

[4:2:66,154] and whether the employee accepted benefits. This data collection is used to report the state's level of ACA compliance to the  

[4:3:66,164] Internal Revenue Service on an annual basis. The state may be assessed penalties for inaccurate reporting (Internal Revenue  

[4:4:66,175] Code sections 6721 and 6722).

[14:0:168,605] 9885   Reserve for Liquidation of Encumbrances  

[14:1:66,627] For individual department budgets, encumbrances (commitments for the procurement of goods or services which have not yet  

[14:2:66,637] been received by the state) are accrued as expenditures by departments at year-end and included in the expenditure totals.  

[14:3:66,647] This treatment is in accordance with the budgetary/legal basis of accounting and consistent with individual department budgets.  

[15:0:66,667] For the purpose of determining the overall General Fund balance, Government Code Section 13307 requires that  

[15:1:66,678] encumbrances should not be counted as a budgetary expenditure until the delivery of the goods and services. Furthermore,  

[15:2:66,688] Generally Accepted Accounting Principles (GAAP) require that encumbrances be reflected as a reserve against the General  

[15:3:66,698] Fund balance and not as an expenditure, as in budgetary/legal basis accounting. Government Code Section 13306 and state  

[15:4:66,708] policy require compliance with GAAP whenever it is in the best interest of the state. This budget reflects a statewide adjustment  

[16:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[3:0:66,83] to reduce expenditures on a budgetary/legal basis by the encumbrance amounts to comply with Government Code Section  

[3:1:66,93] 13307 and GAAP. A reserve of fund balance for encumbrances for this same amount is shown in Summary Schedule 1 for the  

[3:2:66,103] General Fund.

[4:3:66,175] year. The Encumbrance Adjustment Table summarizes the methodology and the calculation for the encumbrance adjustment.

[6:0:162,177] 9889   Public School System Stabilization Account  

[6:1:66,199] Proposition 2, approved by voters in November 2014, established the Public School System Stabilization Account (PSSSA) as  

[6:2:66,209] a ”rainy day“ reserve for K-14 schools.  

[7:0:66,227] Proposition 2 requires Proposition 98 General Fund deposits into or withdrawals from the fund each year, as well as two  

[7:1:66,237] preceding fiscal years, when specific criteria are met.   Calculation of a deposit or withdrawal from the   PSSSA does not change  

[7:2:66,247] the Proposition 98 minimum guarantee calculation.
